### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-09-10
Mac4Lin is back!

This is the version 1.0 Release Candidate. Some components are still under development. Currently the shell script is not able to set the GDM theme, cursor theme, sounds, emerald theme. They need to be manually set.

Also components like Firefox3, Thunderbird theme, awn theme/plugins etc. are still under development. The Mozilla themes may not be stable. Hence use the non-core components of Mac4Lin at your own risk. Documentation is still in the pipeline. I decided to release the RC anyway so that patrons can start using it and update to the stable version when development is complete.

Whats new: Mac4Lin v1.0 RC - 9th September, 2008

New! Automated Installer in the form of a shell script
New GDM theme
Supports the newest version of GNOME and Xfce
New Mozilla themes specifically built for Mac4Lin
Adium style AWN status icons for Pidgin
Mac style scrollbars, menus
Other tweaks in GTK theme
Adium sounds for Pidgin
New usplash

Keeping up the tradition I'm including the download stats. SF.net alone has served about 10.4TB as on today! I'm also happy to announce that Mac4Lin was one of the winners of FOSS Awards 2008.

Instructions:

Download the Mac4Lin_v1.0_RC.tar.gz archive to any folder. Extract the archive and run Mac4Lin_Install_v1.0_RC.sh file.

For any suggestions/comments/complaints/feedback/bug tracking please drop by my blog or send a mail:

My Blog: [http://phoenix-ani.blogspot.com/](http://phoenix-ani.blogspot.com/)
My E-Mail id: infra_red_dude<A.T>users<D.O.T>sourceforge<D.O.T>n et
Project Website: [http://sourceforge.net/projects/mac4lin](http://sourceforge.net/projects/mac4lin)

PS: The old thread at: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=555373](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=555373) was shifted over to the archive section. Hence this new thread.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-09-11
> **kestal said:**
> Out of curiosity to the creators of this, did you activate the keyboard shortcuts (f5/f6 - or whatever) for volume levels with the graphical display that fades in and out?

If so, did you tie it into the mac sound effect?
Err.. No. Thats not possible. You can code an app for that and it'll work great :) But you can assign shortcut for changing volume and if you haf compiz enabled you can get a similar window for controlling the volume but the sound effects are absent.

PS: BTW the keys are F11 and F12 :)

### Post by xinloiemnham2 on 2008-09-13
Hey, I found how to get back shutdown and restart button. Open Login window (system/administration/login window), in Local tab, check Show action menu.

---

### Post by Osvit on 2008-09-13
> **infra_red_dude said:**
> 


Err.. Damn.. that shutdown dialog looks ugly! I did many tests on various platforms and this problem is absent. I'm not sure if the script is the culprit. I'll do all I can to find out more details regarding this.

had the same problem, the issue was in wrong user rights on ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0_RC/ (probably a consequence of running the script in sudo mode? ) The fix is sudo chown -R yourusername:yourgroup ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0_RC/

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-10-10
Unfortunately I tried to add the icons for NM applet. But everytime there is an update the icons get screwed up. There were so many updates that I stopped changing icons for it. So depedning on which version of NM-applet you haf, you may or may not see the icons. Its also possible that the icons maybe visible partially. Frankly, I've no plans to run after the nm-applet fixing icons after every small update.

### Post by cgrenier on 2008-10-22
It's the theme itself, nothing to do with the script.  The version of gtk2-engines-pixbuf in the intrepid repositories is not compatible with the Mac4lin GTK theme.  

Another question: When I decide not to use the Mac4lin metacity theme, how do I get the buttons back to their usual place, with the min-max-close in the upper right?

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-10-22
Follow this: 

> 
Press Alt+F2, type in gconf-editor. Press Enter or click Run and a new window should appear. In the sidebar, go to / &#8594; apps &#8594; metacity &#8594; general. Back on the right hand side, double click on button_layout. Delete the value that's there and type in menu:minimize,maximize,close. Then Click OK and close the application Configuration Editor. The buttons will now be on the left side of titlebar. To restore the original layout, just replace the string with close,minimize,maximize:menu.


Thanks Peng :)

### Post by EnGorDiaz on 2008-10-26
> **infra_red_dude said:**
> Mac4Lin is back!

This is the version 1.0 Release Candidate. Some components are still under development. Currently the shell script is not able to set the GDM theme, cursor theme, sounds, emerald theme. They need to be manually set.

Also components like Firefox3, Thunderbird theme, awn theme/plugins etc. are still under development. The Mozilla themes may not be stable. Hence use the non-core components of Mac4Lin at your own risk. Documentation is still in the pipeline. I decided to release the RC anyway so that patrons can start using it and update to the stable version when development is complete.

Whats new: Mac4Lin v1.0 RC - 9th September, 2008

New! Automated Installer in the form of a shell script
New GDM theme
Supports the newest version of GNOME and Xfce
New Mozilla themes specifically built for Mac4Lin
Adium style AWN status icons for Pidgin
Mac style scrollbars, menus
Other tweaks in GTK theme
Adium sounds for Pidgin
New usplash

Keeping up the tradition I'm including the download stats. SF.net alone has served about 10.4TB as on today! I'm also happy to announce that Mac4Lin was one of the winners of FOSS Awards 2008.

Instructions:

Download the Mac4Lin_v1.0_RC.tar.gz archive to any folder. Extract the archive and run Mac4Lin_Install_v1.0_RC.sh file.

For any suggestions/comments/complaints/feedback/bug tracking please drop by my blog or send a mail:

My Blog: [http://phoenix-ani.blogspot.com/](http://phoenix-ani.blogspot.com/)
My E-Mail id: infra_red_dude<A.T>users<D.O.T>sourceforge<D.O.T>n et
Project Website: [http://sourceforge.net/projects/mac4lin](http://sourceforge.net/projects/mac4lin)

PS: The old thread at: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=555373](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=555373) was shifted over to the archive section. Hence this new thread.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-10-27
> **yanaek said:**
> great job! ;) BUT, i think the new tabs are awful!!, please restore that tabs from Mac4Lin 0.4 , they were perfect, also Distributor Logo.. the one, ubuntu, from Mac4Lin 0.4 was better than that new Gnome foot.
You can put in whatever icon you like for the distributor logo. The reason why it was switched from Ubuntu logo to GNOME was because people using Mac4Lin are on various distros and wanted the logo to be independent of distro.

You can place the logo in the folder ~/.icons/<Mac4Lin folder>/scalable/places. Find and replace all the GNOME foot icons with the one you like.

> **yanaek said:**
> also there is a minor problem with scrollbar in firefox on my system
Yes, its a known issue. We are working on it.

The devs' response to the new bugs? "We've got too many other things to deal with. You'll just have to wait for Firefox 3.0.1 (or so) for us to fix them." (paraphrased)

### Post by Mr.Linc on 2008-11-14
Hi guys,

I've beem usimg mac4lin since v. 0.3 and loved it.

I just switched to Ubuntu 8.10 a week ago and yesterday I installed this mac4lin v 1 RC, I'm using it "clean" (I mean I don't use Compiz and visual effects, just the theme), and found a few problems, most of them already described here in this topic by other people, but I've got a few more comments to let you know:

- Instead of the proper "Computer" icon on desktop, I've got an icon that depicts a blue folder with an "X" on it. :confused:
I looked into the icons folders and that's the one included for "Computer", which is weird; so I had to change it manually.
I don't know if this happens only to me or to someone else.

- Personally (and it's only a matter of tastes) I don't like the installation script. I prefer the manual installation, as on older mac4lin versions.

- At least a README file is much needed; I don't mean to update the whole pdf included on older versions, but at least a small README with a link to this topic and a couple warnings about the few things that may not work properly, would be great and easy to set up.

- Just to let you know, the Clear-type fonts fix doesn't work well on Intrepid (text looks blurry everywhere), at least for some people, so it should be removed from the pack.

- And here's a solution for others who just updated their Ubuntu and got Firefox 3.0.3: the older add-ons and themes don't work, but I found a theme that does work fine on new FF versions:
[https://addons.mozilla.org/firefox/addon/7172](https://addons.mozilla.org/firefox/addon/7172)

Keep up the good work! :)

We jumped to 1.0 because at the time infra started on the update there was very little he could do to add to the pack, other than tweaking some things. Speaking of including everyone, Mac4Lin 1.0 seems to work fine in both GNOME and Xfce. We wanted to make it available to KDE users as well, but nobody answered our call for help to get it KDE-compatible. If anyone wants to help us port Mac4Lin 1.0 to KDE 4 please let infra or I know. We really want everyone to be able to run Mac4Lin, no matter which version of Linux they're running.

### Post by spandanj on 2008-11-17
Hi,

just want to say a few of my thoughts...

Leopard has been here for months now. ie. Mac os Leopard. However, not ONE-single theme for gnome has completely emulated Leopard's look. Different themes - Mac4lin, leopardish, aurora-leopard - have different things that are better than in other themes. eg. I like the "depth" look of buttons in Leopardish, I like the pull-down menu colors in mac4lin. I like how Leopardish works well the global-menu. I like leopardish's metacity theme.


The point is: Not a Single theme is the ultimate at copying Leopard's look. Sadly, it's not because it impossible to do so since each theme has achieved some aspect better than the other. I don't know why it is. But, its been months, and I am still out there Looking for a better leopard theme everyday when the best one could be compiled today if only different leopard themes were to work together and make ONE!!!!

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-11-18
Hello :)

I completely agree with you on the fact that Mac4Lin doesn't bring 100% Mac OS X UI to Linux.

When you ask "Can't xyz be done?" from a user's perspective, I'd say you are not wrong in asking that. Me, being one who codes themes can answer this question from a coder's perspective. Different themes give different levels of accuracy. Each component in a theme is tightly integrated. So to get that certain "abc" you may need to implement the theme in a certain fashion. This means, if you haf "abc" in your theme you may not be able to implement feature "def". 

But yes, with the latest versions of engines it maybe possible to integrate all features. I did try a couple of what you've indicated in your screenshots, but unfortunately it broke the existing elements. Surely, working hard on the current code, I suppose we can achieve the results. We'll prolly haf to re-code all the dependent elements.

I do not rule out including all this in the next version. I will try whatever I can with the limited time I haf.

Cheers :)

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-11-19
> **spandanj said:**
> for Leopard screenshots: [http://www.winsupersite.com/showcase/leopard_screens.asp](http://www.winsupersite.com/showcase/leopard_screens.asp)
Thanks for posting that link. I can't tell you how many times I've had to go hunting for Leopard screenshots to try to see what the original looks like in one circumstance or another.

There's also another issue with trying to copy OSX too carefully. Apple isn't above slapping down people who use their looks, etc. without proper permission. Just in the last year infra and I have talked about the Mac4Lin logo components and what we can and can't use because of ownership/licensing issues. If we try to duplicate the look of OSX too closely we may find that infra's hearing from Apple's lawyers, even if we do manage to keep the changes from borking the rest of the the system.

That said, I look forward to seeing even more of the OSX experience in Linux, especially with projects such as [Gloobus]("http://www.uluga.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=828774") and [Global Menu]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/global_menu") (formerly known as MacMenu).

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-11-19

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-11-21
> **spandanj said:**
> again,

PLEASE infra_red_dude, I will be disappointed if you do not make mac4lin less grey....please.

take a look - [http://www.computerworld.com/action/article.do?command=viewArticleBasic&articleId=9043898&pageNumber=23](http://www.computerworld.com/action/article.do?command=viewArticleBasic&articleId=9043898&pageNumber=23)

- the secondary space is less GREY than main toolbar.

also, DO take a LOOK at the rest of the screenshots!

I really, really hope that the next release is way Better than one we have. there are so many improvements to be made. 

thanks. you are awesome.
I'd like to add a couple of things here. Because of the way GTK and GNOME are built, it is not possible to haf that kind of setup. There are only 2 distinctions here - The metacity theme (which is only the titlebar) and the rest. Leopard is built differently. Here you can haf the same shade for the titlebar as well as the toolbar while hafing a different setup for the rest of the window.

If I make the "secondary" space less gray, then except the titlebar everything else would be white; in which case it will be the same as any of the Mac OS X Tiger themes (which are in plenty).

I hope you get my point.


> **spandanj said:**
> more screenshots for you: [http://www.computerworld.com/action/article.do?command=viewArticleBasic&articleId=9043898](http://www.computerworld.com/action/article.do?command=viewArticleBasic&articleId=9043898)

sadly, they are not full resolution. but, not bad.

also, can you please mac4lin theme less grey...take a look at 2 screenshots I have attached. I like the white version. it's easy on the eyes, and easy to skim over.
To clarify this: The "less gray" window you see (with the dock on the side) is actually not an active window but an inactive one. If you select that window, the it'll be as gray as Leopard is.

And BTW, I use a MacBook Pro. So if anybody is in need to Leopard Screenshots you can ask me :P

> **alex.rayu said:**
> Thank you for creating Mac4Lin.
I'm glad you like Mac4Lin. I appreciate your post :)

> **reddevil2064 said:**
> Not to be a thread crapper but he's doing all of this for free man. So if you want to see some change why don't you get with him and contribute. Giving him suggestions is one thing but basically demanding he change it is going to get you nowhere.
I'd second that! Not that I must be paid or something for my work! :P hehe...  but the fact that anybody is free to join me in making Mac4Lin better. I've always invited people to join in. DJ Peng and Dr.P haf been helping me a lot and one thing I wish to add is that if it weren't for them 1.0 RC would've still been in development! :)

I get a lot of mails everyday to modify Mac4Lin in a certain way. I would love to do that given I haf sufficient time. But thats the whole problem! Since I'm short of time, I decided to develop Mac4Lin based on certain reference. And that reference is Mac OS X Leopard. I try to make Mac4Lin as close as possible. Individual users may haf certain preferences. From a developer's PoV, it is very difficult for me to customize Mac4Lin as per everybody's liking hence I chose the reference. But if anybody requests me to change certain things in Mac4Lin I never fail to reply them with the procedure to follow to make those changes; so that end of the day everybody's happy and gets to learn something new :)

Feel free to mail me. I will do whatever I can to help you customize Mac4Lin to your liking :)

### Post by Crakie on 2008-11-22
Hi guys, another fan here. Excellent work on Mac4Lin1.0RC, I've been installing it today. As a long time KDE user, I did not expect Gnome to feel this intuitive so quickly.

I'm using Ubuntu Intrepid. Just too quick questions:

1) I ran into the 'gtk theme engine is not installed' thingy when selecting the Mac4Lin aqua theme. Is this because these applications are written for an old version of metacity/gtk/whatever, or is the theme not working properly? (Might be a silly question, but I'm a Gnome newbie).

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-11-22

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-11-22
> **Crakie said:**
> Hi guys, another fan here. Excellent work on Mac4Lin1.0RC, I've been installing it today.
Thank you :)

> **Crakie said:**
> 1) I ran into the 'gtk theme engine is not installed' thingy when selecting the Mac4Lin aqua theme. A few posts back it says not to worry about it
Correct! :)

> **Crakie said:**
> ... but some applications (Synaptic, for example) have these 'old fashioned' window decorations, just like Gnome right out of the box. Is this because these applications are written for an old version of metacity/gtk/whatever, or is the theme not working properly?
The two are unrelated. This happens because Synaptic runs in admin mode (notice that this happens with every app which asks for the root password). This happens so coz these apps run under root mode. To fix this, if you can login as root, then set the root's themes to Mac4Lin. A second fix is to simply create links for /root/.thems and /root/.icons to the folders ~/.themes, ~/.icons (meaning linking root's themes and icons folders to the ones in your home folder).

> **Crakie said:**
> 2) Is there any way to remove the white font 'shading' in the window title? It's plain GTK/Metacity (not Emerald/Compiz)?
You need to edit the metacity-1.xml (~/.themes/<Mac4Liin theme>/metacity folder) and change the active window title text color field to whatever you like :)

---

That's the current version. RC1 is the latest testing "build" of Mac4Lin 1.0. Just follow the documentation and you should be all set.

> **Snorlaxative said:**
> Peng, you are getting me really excited to use globalmenu. I have never been able to get it to work, and you're method seems to have gotten me the closest, although I've encountered a problem I hope you can identify and tell me what I'm doing wrong.

When I edit my sources.list I get an error in my terminal saying:
Failed to load module "globalmenu-gnome": libglobalmenu cannot open shared object file: No such file or directory"

And when I try to apt-get install it tells me "couldn't find package gnome2-globalmenu"

What am I doing wrong :confused:

Please help.
What repos did you add? It should be (these are **updated sources** for the GlobalMenu Team's PPA) ```
deb http://ppa.launchpad.net/globalmenu-team/ubuntu intrepid main
deb-src http://ppa.launchpad.net/globalmenu-team/ubuntu intrepid main
```That should be two separate lines. Then run ```
sudo apt-get update
``` (I forgot to put that in my tutorial, but I'll fix that in a sec). Once that's finished then try > sudo apt-get install gnome2-globalmenu You may also want to comment all the lines in ~/.gnomerc before installing gnome2-globalmenu. Let me know how it goes.

### Post by spandanj on 2008-11-30
Hey Anirudh,

Can you include a guide for auto-hinting fonts in ubuntu 8.04 in your documentation. I think it's turned on by default in ubuntu 8.10. Please take a look at the following font files I have attached to this post.

Really, try fonts1.txt yourself. You will see big changes! looks so much better....


1) make a new file '.font.conf' in your home directory
2) copy and paste text from fonts1.txt to .font.conf file
3) log out
4) log in.

Q3: Picking up the pieces of Unix knowledge after 12 years: How hard is it to get going again and install MAC4LIN, where do I start?

Many thanks in advance.
Thank you. Glad you liked Mac4Lin! :)

1) Yes it does. Its architecture independent. The only pre-req. is a GTK based DE.

2) As I said, it runs on any Operating System with GTK based DE (even openSolaris!)

3) Its as easy as executing this script: ./Mac4Lin_v1.0_install.sh!!!! Just download the 3 files on Mac4Lin's sourceforge.net website and go thru the PDF documentation if you wanna do the extra stuff installation. For basic install, extracting the main Mac4Lin tar.gz archive and just executing the script will do the job! :)

> **ardchoille42 said:**
> You're welcome


1) Ok, I'll just wait until it's changed in the Mac4Lin project as I can't figure out how to fix it.

2) Hey, thanks for the info about the graphics, I made the change. Some apps don't look good with this and some do (gedit looks great but messageboxes don't). Perhaps this is why the Mac4Lin devs didn't do it ;)

Keep up the great work, looking forward to the next Mac4Lin release :)
Thank you :) Yep, thats the reason why I didn't change the color or the shade of gray. Believe me, I've tested the shade of gray for months before arriving at this decision!

> **spandanj said:**
> Hey Anirudh,

Can you include a guide for auto-hinting fonts in ubuntu 8.04 in your documentation. I think it's turned on by default in ubuntu 8.10. Please take a look at the following font files I have attached to this post.

Really, try fonts1.txt yourself. You will see big changes! looks so much better....


1) make a new file '.font.conf' in your home directory
2) copy and paste text from fonts1.txt to .font.conf file
3) log out
4) log in.

Thanks man! 
Let me know how I can help with the theme. I don't own a mac.

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-12-01
There's also the fact that Safari is a very different browser from Firefox, and running it on under WINE would make you need to get updates every time Apple fixes a security issue. For my money I'd rather run a Linux browser, even if I do wish there were a better alternative to Firefox 3.

@infra:
I need to see what I can do to theme Evolution better but I'm afraid it takes GTK widgets so we may not have the option of theming it as closely as we can Firefox.

### Post by ardchoille42 on 2008-12-01
Heads up:

I like to use gftp for ftp work and I am using gftp 2.0.18 on Ubuntu 8.10 (Intrepid). When you start gftp it themes fine, but when you change directories in either pane, the text in the listviews is blank, although the icons are still there and scrolling makes text appear for the items you scroll into view, but text disappears once you change dirs again. You can click next to an icon, where the text is supposed to be, and still change directories or do file work, it's just that the text is blank. Also, all of the menus have a dotted line at the top of each menu once the menu is dropped down (I use Global Menu so I don't know if this menu problem is with GM or Mac4Lin).

Just wanted to let infra_red_dude know about this in case he can get this fixed.

[COLOR="Red"]UPDATE[/COLOR]:
I did some troubleshooting and found that this is not a problem with the Mac4Lin theme package as the problem is also seen when using the default (shipped) theme for Ubuntu. I'm now thinking it is a problem with Intrepid or Compiz, and I have filed a bug in Launchpad with all relevant information.

When I disabled Compiz I was able to see the text without a problem until they fixed a bug in the video drivers.

### Post by spandanj on 2008-12-02
**#1 suggestions: window border (metacity)**

a) thinner Bottom border of metacity border. Can you make it as thin as the sides? 
b) In a dark wallpaper, the corners of the metacity window border look weird because you can see the very smooth curve of the corner and pixels....so if you make the corners tight as well, that would be great.

**#2 suggestions: MacOSX theme for firefox 3**

a) Can you add the "adjust window size" icon in the bottom right corner of the status bar in the firefox 3 theme. For example, take a look at iFox metal theme for firefox.
b) icons for right-click menu on a webpage. eg. icon for 'save image as', or for 'copy link location', etc

**#3 suggestions: Gtk theme**

a) align text in the status bar of nautilus to center
b) 3d press down (eg. leopardish) effects in nautilus tabs
c) aqua look on nautilus "view as icons' menu
d) aqua bars for nautilus "name, size, type, date modified" in _List_ view.
e) thin border between "places" and actual folder space in nautilus
f) provide a default ".font.conf" optimized to go with mac4lin

[B]
+4: panel [/B]

a)...transparent/leopard panel for aqua theme.

I hope you are doing your best to make mac4lin an exact replica of mac leopard, or as _*close *_as possible!

thanks.

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-12-04
Just an FYI but the Mozilla devs are at it again. When Firefox 3.2 comes out there will be [a number of changes]("http://forums.mozillazine.org/viewtopic.php?f=18&t=975065") to how themes work. They've recently split the Mozilla 1.9.1/Firefox 3.1 branch from the programming trunk and I'm seeing some changes already in how the master theme is coded. There were [9 pages of changes to themes]("http://forums.mozillazine.org/viewtopic.php?f=18&t=665138") for Firefox 3.1 so we'll need to double check the Mac4Lin Firefox themes as we get closer to 3.1 coming out to see what breaks in our themes. Sine it's Firefox themes I have no doubt we'll probably have to tweak some things to resolve bugs they added for us. If you're testing Firefox 3.1 please let us know how the themes are working in comparison to Firefox 3.0.4 so we start getting an idea what we may need to do.

@infra:
And you thought GNOME devs were bad about changing themes with updates. ;)

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-12-04
Mac4Lin 1.0 RC is actually an outdated build. You should try RC1 (if that's not what you have), but infra's updating RC1 to include themes that have been updated to work with Firefox 3.0.4. I can't tell if he's posted them to the server at SourceForge yet but he's got a lot on his plate with the end of the semester. If he hasn't posted them yet you should get the Nightly Tester Tools extensions that I [mentioned]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6296030&postcount=195") back on page 20. You can use that to override the compatibility check on the themes. The only thing missing is a bump of the maxversion, the highest version of Firefox that the themes work with. You can seafely override the version check on our themes until infra gets the RC updated.

I found it pretty slow in performance but that's just me since I have really optimised my graphics for application performance. Perhaps it may help obtaining some icons & skins from there?

sudo ./*.sh
```in the right folder, instead.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-12-05
That is normal if you don't haf any artwork installed in your home folder. Just create .themes, .icons, .emerald (if you use Emerald Theme Manager) in your home folder and the script will do the rest. Otherwise you can always do the manual installation as explained the PDF documentation :)

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-12-06
> **infra_red_dude said:**
> That is normal if you don't haf any artwork installed in your home folder. Just create .themes, .icons, .emerald (if you use Emerald Theme Manager) in your home folder and the script will do the rest. Otherwise you can always do the manual installation as explained the PDF documentation :)
Thanks for posting that. I wasn't aware the directories may not be created automatically. I'll add that to the docs.

> **ardchoille42 said:**
> Yeah, that's the one I had been using, but the top level menu item text goes blank on mouse-over.. yours don't do that :)
That's a known issue in the MacOSX Theme. DrP fixed it for us. :)

> **KEE said:**
> ok how do I uninstall this? its not like the document at all =/ there are no Mac4Lin_Aqua and Mac4Lin_Graphite themes and searched for it. please help
I beg to differ. In the Mac4Lin 1.0 RC1 folder (where I extracted it to) there's a folder called GTK, which has these files:
```
peng@IceBox-Hardy:~/Mac4Lin/Mac4Lin_v1.0_RC1/GTK$ dir
Mac4Lin_GTK_Graphite_v1.0_RC.tar.gz     Mac4Lin_MacMenu_v1.0_RC.tar.gz
Mac4Lin_GTK_v1.0_RC.tar.gz         Mac4Lin_Meta_v1.0_RC.tar.gz
Mac4Lin_MacMenu_Graphite_v1.0_RC.tar.gz
peng@IceBox-Hardy:~/Mac4Lin/Mac4Lin_v1.0_RC1/GTK$ 

```Those 11 files are in the /GTK directory of the Mac4Lin 1.0 RC1 archive. As for uninstalling, there's an uninstall script, but it could blow away your Mac4Lin working folders. You may want to move the files you downloaded from our SourceForge site to another directory for safe keeping, unless you just want to download them again at a later date.

> **KEE said:**
> ok that worked but there was a name changed its not *RC1 its just *RC, I think the file is named that way too. heres what i got so far

```
 root@root-desktop:~/Desktop/Mac4Lin_v1.0_RC1$ sudo ./Mac4Lin_Install_v1.0_RC.sh
...

```there is some errors in here is this normal? lol
I'm curious why you're logged in as root. That's a very bad idea from a security standpoint and really shouldn't be done. Ever. Ubuntu gives you tools to for users to use to temporarily grant you root access. As far as running the script as the root user goes it could be generating unintended issues. Running the script with sudo is unnecessary. When it comes time to need root level access it asks for your sudo password.

> **KEE said:**
> infra_red_dude  suggested that I follow the PDF file, thats like the first step, but theres no GTK Metacity Theme
Again, you're logged in as root, which is a very bad idea and could be causing more problems than it fixes. If you have a regular user account please log in with that account and see if the script runs better. And as I pasted above there should be 11 items in that folder. If you don't have them than you may need to download the RC1.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-12-06
^^^ I haf absolutely no idea regarding this error. I'm seeing this for the first time. Lemme see if I can dig out something.

What I'm assuming is that you are not setting the correct Cursor theme in Compiz configuration settings manager. In the general tab, there is an entry for the Cursor theme. Try changing the name there to Mac4Lin cursor theme, then logout and log back in. May fix things.

### Post by lime4x4 on 2008-12-07
2.2 Shifting the order of the titlebar buttons
         The installation script will move the “traffic lights”, the minimize, maximize
         and close buttons, on the left hand side of the titlebar in Metacity
         (instructions for using the Emerald/Compiz Fusion theme appear in Section
3). If you want to make the change manually, press Alt+F2 and type in gconf-editor.
Press Enter or click Run and a new window should appear. In the sidebar, go to / &#8594;
apps &#8594; metacity &#8594; general. Back on the right hand side, double click on
button_layout. Delete the value that's there and type in
menu:minimize,maximize,close. Then Click OK and close the application
Configuration Editor. The buttons will now be on the left side of titlebar. To restore
the buttons to the original layout, just replace the string with
close,minimize,maximize:menu.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-12-08
If you are using Emerald themer then following the first part will not help because that is not not all used.

With emerald to shift the buttons to the right, you need to select the Mac4Lin emerald theme and goto theme settings > title bar layout and select the normal format (it would be set to OSX be default).

PS: Peng, I guess we need t include this too alongwith the metacity button layout change in FAQ.

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-12-09
> **TheMacFactor said:**
> I have followed this to the letter, and the buttons resolutely remain on the right hand side of the window.

Also, following your instructions:

Emerald Theme Manager installs without any preloaded themes.

Any ideas?

**EDIT**

Since I wrote this, I went to find an emerald OSX theme that might fit the bill, and when I got back to the Emerald Theme Manager, the default themes were sitting there! Maybe if I can find some sort of displacement activity, the buttons will suddenly shift to the left of the window...
Ah, you're trying to switch them in *Emerald*, not GTK. That makes a big difference. To switch the Emerald traffic lights open the Emerald Theme Manager, then select the theme and switch to the Edit Themes > Titlebar. You'll see a text box about halfway down on the right labeled Title-bar Object Layout. You can change that field to change the order things appear on the titlebar. When I switch the traffic lights back I use

```
HM:I(5)T:N(5)X(5)C
```You can put that in any order you want, and there's a legend key right below the text box to show what everything is.

I just realized I hadn't included it in the docs. I'll make sure I get it in there. *Sorry 'bout that!*

> **infra_red_dude said:**
> If you are using Emerald themer then following the first part will not help because that is not not all used.

With emerald to shift the buttons to the right, you need to select the Mac4Lin emerald theme and goto theme settings > title bar layout and select the normal format (it would be set to OSX be default).

PS: Peng, I guess we need t include this too alongwith the metacity button layout change in FAQ.

### Post by ardchoille42 on 2008-12-10
> **rausuar said:**
> Hi !!!

First of all, I would like thank and congratulate the developers and contributers of this great theme. Personally, I think it makes a great difference from the plain aspect of the desktop we all see when we first install our versions of Linux.

If any one can help me, it would be good.

Thanks again!

I feel the best compliments to Mac4Lin are the GlobalMenu and Avant Window Navigator. [Here is a screenshot]("http://ardchoille.nfshost.com/Gallery/Screenshots?action=imagelink&i=scr-20081125.jpg") of my current desktop using both with the Mac4Lin package (please forgive the .jpg quality).

Since you're using Ubuntu 8.10, the Avant Window Navigator is easy to install, simply enable the universe repo and do:

```

sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install avant-window-navigator awn-applets-c-extras awn-applets-python-extras

```

Once it's installed, you can run it from Applications > Accessories > Avant Window Navigator. More themes for awn can be found [here]("http://wiki.awn-project.org/Themes").

The GlobalMenu thread is located [here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=241868").

First of all, I would like thank and congratulate the developers and contributers of this great theme. Personally, I think it makes a great difference from the plain aspect of the desktop we all see when we first install our versions of Linux.

If any one can help me, it would be good.

Thanks again!

Thank you :)

> **rausuar said:**
> Thanks ardchoille42,

I saw your screen shot, very nice.  I want to know which are the applications and how you configure the icons you have in your awn (i mean, the ones you have in your screenshot)!

In the other hand, well, I was referring with my original post to the desktop effects of compiz, for example, I have seen in the macs that there is a wall where you can see in a minor view all the open windows in your desktop, etc.  I know there are some around, but could you help me with that?

thanks!
First of all you need to find out if the graphics driver supported Compiz. If it does, then all you need to do is right click on your desktop > Change background > Goto the desktop effects tab and enable it from there! Also install compizconfiguration settings manager from synaptic to haf total control over everything.

The plugin you are talking about is either Expose or Virtual desktop (workspaces) which will be enabled when you enable the desktop effects. If you know which graphics card you use, you can simply google for <graphic card> + compiz + ubuntu and you are most likely to get a step by step guide on enabling desktop effects, if your gfx card supports compiz. Hope that was helpful :)

### Post by ardchoille42 on 2008-12-11
> **DJ_Peng said:**
> I doubt that's a Mac4Lin issue, but it may be a rendering issue. What type of video card are you running? If you're running Compiz you may want to try disabling it temporarily (using the Compiz Fusion Icon from the repos) and see if that has any effect. I know I was having a devil of a time with seeing fonts in WINE apps due to an issue with my Nvidia driver and Compiz. When I disabled Compiz I was able to see the text without a problem until they fixed a bug in the video drivers.

After a bit of troubleshooting, I have found it is not an issue with Mac4Lin, as the problem persists when using the default Ubuntu Human theme. I've filed a bug in Launchpad so the Ubuntu devs can handle it. Sorry for the false alarm.

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-12-13
Actually I think he may be referring to the slight transparency. That's one of the cool features in OSX Leopard but it doesn't work as well in Ubuntu because you can end up with part of the panel transparent and some not. You can try it for yourself by clicking on an open section of the top panel > Preferences > Background, then select a solid color rather than an image and play with the style slider. I disabled it because too many of my applets force the background color.

I'm noticing when I call up that dialog that dialog that I get an error that "The folder contents could not be displayed". Are we ding the panel background differently this version? The specific message it gives me is
> Error stating the file 'home/peng/.themes/
Mac4Lin_GTK_Graphite_v.04/gtk-2.0/
Panel': No such file or directoryI know the directory got blown away when I used the M4L 1.0 RC uninstall script, but shouldn't there be something in 1.0 RC1 to specify which file is used for the background?

It's almost as if the start graphic is cutting off some of the shading on the right hand side of the checkbox. Come to think of it, it maybe a Compiz issue.

> **ssthormess said:**
> Hey, i really like Mac4Lin, but, i have some questions:

 (a) Where are ubicated the "icons"? (i want to replace some)
 (b) Where is ubicated the gnome-panel background (i deleted my panel for making a new one and the new panel doesnt show it).
 (c) When i installed Mac4Lin the Ubuntu Boot Screen (when loads and says Ubuntu with a progress bar) and now my LCD can't handle it (AOC LW97 19'', SiS Integrated Videocard (a.k.a. ****))
 (d) Do you plan to create more skins for other apps (like EMESENE or SONGBIRD)?
 
Thanks from Venezuela :)
(a) ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0_RC
(b) ~/.themes/Mac4Lin_GTK_v1.0_RC/gtk-2.0/Panel (although it may be a different subdirectory under .themes depending on which theme you have active
(c) The boot splash (Usplash) has known issues, which I'm currently working on. You should use a different usplash until I post a working usplash for Mac4Lin. Anything else could be a video driver issue.
(d) Each new theme requires someone with the time and energy to create it. I wouldn't know where to begin with a Songbird theme (I use Sonata and Amarok 2) but having worked on Firefox themes in the past I can tell you that it takes quite a bit of work to create a single theme, even when you use an existing theme as a starting point. We welcome anyone's help in creating new components for Mac4Lin, so if you're willing to give it a shot we'd be happy to share the fruits of your labors. Although you want want to keep a bottle of Tylenol/Ibuprophen/[YourFavoriteOverTheCounterHeadacheRemedy] handy, because I'm sure you'll need it. ;)

The second one is new. In v0.4, the Unlock screen was awesome: It was Mac OS X-ish and it floated above the screensaver, letting you unlock your computer while watching your badass screensaver. Now, here's how the unlock screen looks like to me: [http://upload.gaiatools.com/files/Lockscreen_0.png](http://upload.gaiatools.com/files/Lockscreen_0.png). The same sleek modal dialog, but on an almost-completely-gray background (with a little gradient thing on top). It's not that bad, but I was used to keep looking at my screensaver :(

### Post by phonicboom on 2008-12-21
> **phonicboom said:**
> How can I tell AWN not to take focus or tell Global Menu not to display AWN? 


Go here CompizConfig Settings Manager > Window Management > Window Rules 

look for No Focus and Press [SIZE="4"]+[/SIZE] then choose Grab, then click on AWN so this 

**class=Avant-window-navigator**

(with Cairo Dock it seems to have to be this **title=**cairo-dock)

appears in the value box

it's not perfect but close

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-12-21
That's a great tip! Thanks for sharing it with us.

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-12-24
> **killer2239 said:**
> First off i love this theme. Hope it gets to 1.0 final.

How do i make firefox up/down be on top and bottom, instead of the up being above the down on the bottom right hand side of the slider bar to the right?
You can try a different Firefox theme. Some themes you may want to try are the [MacOSX Theme]("https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/7172") (the basis for our Fx3 theme), [Proto]("https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/7540"), the [iFox themes]("http://www.radar.250x.com/tb.html"), and the [VFox|FINDER]("http://vsdigital.deviantart.com/art/VFoxFINDER2-Firefox-Skin-63816222") theme. I can't say any of those themes split the scrollbar arrows, but you can check them out. Just don't use any of the [GrApple themes]("http://www.takebacktheweb.org/") unless you're running them on a Mac. They may work but Aronnax!, the developer of those themes, says they may have unintended results, including possibly borking your Firefox installation and profiles beyond any possibility of use.

> **ardchoille42 said:**
> Actually, the way the scroll buttons look in the current firefox theme in Mac4Lin is the way OSX does it, both the up and down buttons are located at the bottom of the scrollbar.. see the attached screenshot.
That's one area where some people may not want to stick quite so closely to the OSX behaviors. Some people won't like having the buttons away from how they're used to doing it. I actually modified the Emerald themes to move the traffic lights to the other side because having them in the OSX order was damned comfusing to this longtime Windows user. But that's the joy of the open source movement. We try to let the user decide how they want to use their computers, rather than shoving *our way* down their throats like MS and Apple can do (and Firefox3 devs seem to want to do).

> **ardchoille42 said:**
> Mac4Lin dev team: How hard would it be to make the toolbar buttons and the urlbar square to more closely match the safari look (attached screenshot)?
Just a thought.
I was thinking our scrollbar arrows were off but having not used a Mac in several years I didn't know if they changed that or not.

### Post by COLiNx86 on 2008-12-24
I just discovered something that could help make your computer more like a mac. I apologize if this has already been posted.
**Making the magic lamp effect in compiz just like OSX.**
1. stop compiz. (if I remember right, in Ubuntu you can just go to appearance, choose effects, and click none, or off. sorry I don't use ubuntu so it may not be dead on but you can probly get the point)
2. First open up a hex editor (ghex) as root. (sudo ghex2 in the terminal)
3. open up the file /usr/lib/compiz/libanimation.so
4. Search (ctrl + f) for the line magic_lamp_max_waves
5. find the value <min>3</min>, it should be RIGHT after magic_lamp_max_waves
6. change the 3 to a 0
7. Save and close
8. Now in a terminal type sudo gedit /usr/share/compiz/animation.xml
9. Search for magic_lamp_max_waves again.
10. now scroll down a few lines untill you see <min>3</min> 
11. once again change the 3 to a 0
12. save and close.
13. reboot.
And I can confirm this working in Arch+Gnome 2.24.2+Compiz-Fusion, but it should work fine in anything that uses gnome 2.24 and a fairly recent compiz.

---

### Post by ardchoille42 on 2008-12-24
> **COLiNx86 said:**
> I just discovered something that could help make your computer more like a mac. I apologize if this has already been posted.
**Making the magic lamp effect in compiz just like OSX.**
1. stop compiz. (if I remember right, in Ubuntu you can just go to appearance, choose effects, and click none, or off. sorry I don't use ubuntu so it may not be dead on but you can probly get the point)
2. First open up a hex editor (ghex) as root. (sudo ghex2 in the terminal)
3. open up the file /usr/lib/compiz/libanimation.so
4. Search (ctrl + f) for the line magic_lamp_max_waves
5. find the value <min>3</min>, it should be RIGHT after magic_lamp_max_waves
6. change the 3 to a 0
7. Save and close
8. Now in a terminal type sudo gedit /usr/share/compiz/animation.xml
9. Search for magic_lamp_max_waves again.
10. now scroll down a few lines untill you see <min>3</min> 
11. once again change the 3 to a 0
12. save and close.
13. reboot.
And I can confirm this working in Arch+Gnome 2.24.2+Compiz-Fusion, but it should work fine in anything that uses gnome 2.24 and a fairly recent compiz.

The trouble with using a hex editor to edit things outside $HOME is those edits will likely be gone if there are any updates to the package that provides the files you edited. Just FYI.

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-12-24
> **infra_red_dude said:**
> [quote=DJ_Peng;6429523]Just don't use any of the [GrApple themes]("http://www.takebacktheweb.org/") unless you're running them on a Mac. They may work but Aronnax!, the developer of those themes, says they may have unintended results, including possibly borking your Firefox installation and profiles beyond any possibility of use.
They work ok and don't break anything. Just that since OS X has a separate menu bar on the top, GrApple themes do not take care of that on Linux and Windows.[/quote]
When I emailed Aronnax about it this back in June this is what he told me.
> Hi,
95% percent from the theme code is platform independent,
but is use although lot of special Mac code which can`t  work on different platforms and it has nothing special for Windows/Linux.
For some parts on Windows/Linux has it nothing and it work then only random or even not at all.

It works better on Linux than on Windows but for sure not as it should be.
And by the way, works it very different on the different Windows versions and maybe the same on Linux.

Or in other words:
It is not a good idea to use it on Windows/Linux.Based on that I said they should be avoided at all costs on Linux due to possibly borking things. I may have exaggerated, but the dev himself said not to use them so I take that with a good bit of authority.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2008-12-30
That issue maybe the way GTK widgets are used in the application but not coz of the Emerald theme for sure. Thats because the Emerald theme does not haf access to the GUI components beyond the Titlebar, the side and the bottom borders. Thats all an Emerald theme is about.

But I can guarantee that nautilus, openoffice etc. work flawlessly with the current GTK/Emerald themes. 

I'd surely like to see your screenshots. That'd help a lot :)

---

### Post by yanaek on 2008-12-31
> **Cavalierski said:**
> 
Still suspend icon is not shown though. Hopefully it will be fixed soon as well ;-)

sleep.svg  and .png icons are solution for this problem
you can copy for example 'scalable/actions/sleep.svg' , '48/actions/sleep.png' and '32/actions/sleep.png' from another theme, like Human (/usr/share/icons/Human/), to Mac4Lin icons folder and voila, you now have Suspend icon in Shutdown gnome menu

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-01-02
The FF3 themes (which *really* should be labeled Fx3) are compatible with Firefox 3.0.x as long as you have my updated themes rather than the ones originally packaged in the RC. The date modified should be around 3 Dec (or whatever date I posted the themes to this thread).

### Post by razor7 on 2009-01-02
> **andresmh said:**
> Where is the theme compatible with Firefox 3.0.5? I unpacked Mac4Lin_Mozilla_v1.0_RC.tar.gz and I found these files:

FF2Extensions
FireFox Safari Theme - Vfox2.jar
Mac4Lin_1.0.1b_FF3_Aqua.jar
Mac4Lin_1.0.1b_FF3_Graphite.jar
Mac4Lin_1.0b_FF3_Graphite.jar
Mac4Lin_1.0b_FF3.jar

None of them open in FF3

Fission - [https://addons.mozilla.org/es-ES/firefox/addon/1951](https://addons.mozilla.org/es-ES/firefox/addon/1951)
Stop-Reload Button - [https://addons.mozilla.org/es-ES/firefox/addon/313](https://addons.mozilla.org/es-ES/firefox/addon/313)
Custom Buttons - [https://addons.mozilla.org/es-ES/firefox/addon/2707](https://addons.mozilla.org/es-ES/firefox/addon/2707)
Hide Menubar - Cant find it, but is unussable anyway, because global_menu widget only works with GTK apps ([https://wiki.ubuntu.com/global_menu](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/global_menu))

The themes need to be updated so Firefox installs them, to do so while the developers update them, just follow this steps:
[LIST=1]
[*]Unpack the contents one of the themes IE: Mac4Lin_1.0.1b_FF3_Aqua.jar
[*]look for the file install.rdf and open it with GEDIT or something else
[*]Search this line <em:maxVersion>3.0</em:maxVersion>
[*]Change it to <em:maxVersion>3.0.10</em:maxVersion>
[*]Repack it  to .jar or .zip and then rename the file to .jar
[*]Drag and drop the file into firefox and install it, it should be no issues at all
[/LIST]

With this you are saying firefox that this extension should work up to version 3.0.10

Do the same to the other themes if you want to.

### Post by Psyphre on 2009-01-07
> **DJ_Peng said:**
> That's the current version. RC1 is the latest testing "build" of Mac4Lin 1.0. Just follow the documentation and you should be all set.


What repos did you add? It should be ```
deb http://ppa.launchpad.net/gnome2-globalmenu/ubuntu intrepid main
deb-src http://ppa.launchpad.net/gnome2-globalmenu/ubuntu intrepid main
```That should be two separate lines. Then run ```
sudo apt-get update
``` (I forgot to put that in my tutorial, but I'll fix that in a sec). Once that's finished then try  You may also want to comment all the lines in ~/.gnomerc before installing gnome2-globalmenu. Let me know how it goes.


That's cool! I'll have to check that out. Thanks for sharing it!

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-01-07

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-01-08
> **Psyphre said:**
> Hi, Ive been using mac menu for a long time with no issues. However last night i installed intrepid and tried to install the  mac menu via PPA. Just likc  snorlax I too get:
couldn't find package gnome2-globalmenu

I  have no idea why! Will be so grateful to anyone who knows how to solve this problem.

Thanks in advance.
I just checked and was reminded that I had to change the PPA for GlobalMenu. If you're running Intrepid you should use the [PPA for the GlobalMenu Team]("https://launchpad.net/%7Eglobalmenu-team/+archive").
```
deb http://ppa.launchpad.net/globalmenu-team/ubuntu intrepid main
deb-src http://ppa.launchpad.net/globalmenu-team/ubuntu intrepid main
```
I know the other sources are the ones that the GlobalMenu wiki on Google Code says to use, but the Launchpad PPA seems to work better.

My apologies to all for not remembering to edit my earlier instructions. I'll go fix that.

---

### Post by Psyphre on 2009-01-08

DJ-peng:
Thanks, I will try those next time but fortunately its been solved! I asked on the global menu thread and no-one knew why it wasnt seeing the package so someone gave me the deb file to install manually. Worked perfectly!

### Post by petit_prince on 2009-02-03
> **infra_red_dude said:**
> But a lot of new users requested for automated install since they were lost reading the exhaustive documentation.
I see your point, infra_red_dude. However, using ```
dpkg -i *<name of package>*
```, the install script could still rely on deb-Packages. That way, you'd only need to script the user-specific settings (i.e. enabling the theme and such) -- and the of us who prefer to do things manually could just use the deb-Packages. How does that sound?

> **infra_red_dude said:**
> Oh btw, don't worry. Nothing would be compromised as far as clean themes are concerned! :)

> **DJ_Peng said:**
> The lower corners in RC2 look rounded to me, but when I pull it up on a dark background I'm not 100% sure about that.

As far as the menu borders being round is concerned they are not actually round. Thats just an illusion. Unfortunately the GTK (and pixmap) does not allow rounded corners. What I've done is just some "ghetto" work in gimp which kinda hides the pointy corners on a light surface. Hence on a dark surface you can see the actual rectangular menu whereas on a light background the "pointy" corners blend with the background. Thats just a GIMP trick ;)

### Post by joshsmith on 2009-02-13
infra_red_dude, why not make the development process of mac4lin more open? 

you could have the code hosted in subversion on google code or bazaar on launchpad. People would have access to code directly and be able to get the benefits of newer features, and you would benefit from powerful bug reporting and fixing system, from other people helping to contribute to the project (if you wanted them to), and from having your work safely stored away from your computer in case something goes wrong

no one will mind if the subversion revisions arent release quality, just getting access to the option of newer (and maybe better) code is enough. 

it would take a very small effort to put your code into subversion once, and then sync it every few days

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-02-19
Thanks for that, MedellinManDem. I ran a locate on my system and came up with this:
> :~$ locate audio-volume-high.svg
/home/peng/awn-extras/awn-applets/awn-extras-applets/src/volume-control/Themes/Black/audio-volume-high.svg
/home/peng/awn-extras/awn-applets/awn-extras-applets/src/volume-control/Themes/Tango/audio-volume-high.svg
/usr/share/icons/Neu/scalable/status/audio-volume-high.svg
/usr/share/icons/gnome/scalable/status/audio-volume-high.svg@Ani:
The path you're looking for is /usr/share/icons/gnome/scalable/status. I'm showing four svg icons in that directory: audio-volume-high.svg, audio-volume-low.svg, audio-volume-medium.svg, audio-volume-muteed.svg

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-02-20
[Ubuntu Tweak 0.4.5]("http://ubuntu-tweak.com/2009/02/14/ubuntu-tweak-045-released.html") is supposed to be able to change the Main Menu icon, but when I tried it with the RC(2) themes this morning the icon didn't change. I filed bug [#332142]("https://bugs.launchpad.net/bugs/332142") Ubuntu Tweak 0.4.5 cannot change the Main Menu icon on third-party themes against UTweak, but it may be an issue about how we store our icons.

ETA: I just stumbled across a Guifications theme for Pidgin that y'all may want to try out: [OSX Theme]("http://sourceforge.net/tracker/index.php?func=detail&aid=1507861&group_id=92888&atid=676821"). It's only dependency is the Guifications plugin for Pidgin, and you install it by extracting it to ~/.purple/guifications/themes and them select the theme in the Guifications config window.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-02-23
Oh I see what you wanna do. For that you will need to modify a number of files. I'm giving you the relative paths under the folder <Mac4Lin Theme>/gtk-2.0/:

1) grayscale.png
2) graystretch.png
3) Toolbar/grayscale.png
4) Toolbar/toolbar.png
5) Toolbar/toolbar1.png
5) Menu-Menubar/menubar.png

You may want to increase the brightness/change shade to alter the gray to your liking.

Hope that helps :)

---

### Post by pickarooney on 2009-02-24

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-02-24
That will only alter the color of menubar (File, Edit menu etc.). To change the color of the whole UI you will need to edit all of the files I've mentioned.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-02-28
I'm happy to inform you all that Mac4Lin now uses the SVN version control system. The latest version Mac4Lin v1.0 RC2 is available there. Users may checkout to download the bleeding edge version.

The required info is provided here:

Subversion Server: [https://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net](https://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net)

Path to Repository: /svnroot/mac4lin

Access instructions:

To access a Subversion repository, configure your Subversion client as follows:

* Hostname: mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net
* Port: 443
* Protocol: HTTPS
* Repository Path: /svnroot/mac4lin

For clients that use a URL string:

[https://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/mac4lin](https://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/mac4lin)

Mac4Lin v1.0RC2 has not been released and hence is not available on the Downloads page. It can only be obtained through SVN. Comments, suggestions, complaints are welcome as always :)

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-03-09
> **thrasher6900 said:**
> I TOTALLY do not understand what to do still.

Could you go into details on what exactly to enter in the terminal to get the update?

I'd appreciate it if you can do so.  Even if it's an email.
Sure I will do that :)

Install subversion on Ubuntu from terminal: sudo apt-get install subversion 

You can then run 'svn' to pull the files from the repo: svn checkout [https://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/mac4lin](https://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/mac4lin)

This will download all the files from SVN to ~/mac4lin folder. Do note that these files are decompressed. So you will need to put the folders in appropriate folders (like the Mac4Lin Icons folder to ~/.icons, the various GTK themes folder in ~/.themes and so on). Or you can compress the folders in .tar.gz and install using Appearances Dialog box as you would install any other UI theme.

Hope that helps :)

PS: I've blogged about using subversion so that more people can pull down the Mac4Lin v1.0 RC2 file and here. Head here: [http://phoenix-ani.blogspot.com/2009/03/howto-use-subversion-and-install.html](http://phoenix-ani.blogspot.com/2009/03/howto-use-subversion-and-install.html)

---

### Post by thrasher6900 on 2009-03-09
> **infra_red_dude said:**
> Sure I will do that :)

Install subversion on Ubuntu from terminal: sudo apt-get install subversion 

You can then run 'svn' to pull the files from the repo: svn checkout [https://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/mac4lin](https://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/mac4lin)

This will download all the files from SVN to ~/mac4lin folder. Do note that these files are decompressed. So you will need to put the folders in appropriate folders (like the Mac4Lin Icons folder to ~/.icons, the various GTK themes folder in ~/.themes and so on). Or you can compress the folders in .tar.gz and install using Appearances Dialog box as you would install any other UI theme.

Hope that helps :)

PS: I've blogged about using subversion so that more people can pull down the Mac4Lin v1.0 RC2 file and here. Head here: [http://phoenix-ani.blogspot.com/2009/03/howto-use-subversion-and-install.html](http://phoenix-ani.blogspot.com/2009/03/howto-use-subversion-and-install.html)Aright that worked. . ....getting it that is.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-03-09
No, you just cannot tar up the whole folder. You need to individually tar the GTK theme folders, Icon theme folder and then install via the Appearances dialog. Try it. If it doesn't work then just head to the link on my blog in my previous post. Hopefully you'll be able to install it :)

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-03-17
I put together a bash script to get the latest Subversion files. It's not perfect, and I'm sure there are things I need to fix, but I wanted to put this up so you guys can use it and be able to point out where I need to fix something. The script assumes that you are snagging the svn files into a folder off your /home directory that is identified as ~/Mac4Lin/svn.

Create a blank document in your [FONT=Courier New]/home[/FONT] folder called [FONT=Courier New]update_mac4lin.sh[/FONT] and put the following into the new file using your favorite text editor
```
#!/bin/bash
cd ~/Mac4Lin/svn
echo "Updating the svn files..."
svn co http://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/mac4lin
echo "Removing the old icon, cursor and theme files"
rm -r -I ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0_RC2
rm -r -I ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Cursors_v1.0_RC2
rm -r -I ~/.themes/Mac4Lin_*
echo "Updating the icon set..."
mkdir ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0 >> null
cp -u -r ~/Mac4Lin/svn/mac4lin/Icons/Mac4Lin_Icons/* ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0_RC2
echo "Updating the cursors..."
mkdir ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Cursors_v1.0 >> null
cp -u -r ~/Mac4Lin/svn/mac4lin/Cursor/Mac4Lin_Cursors/* ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Cursors_v1.0_RC2
echo "Updating the themes..."
cp -u -r ~/Mac4Lin/svn/mac4lin/GTK/Mac4Lin_* ~/.themes/
echo "Opening the Appearances window so you can verify the new theme and components"
gnome-appearance-properties
cd ~
```Save the file, and make it executable with
```
sudo chmod a+x ~/update_mac4lin.sh
```Simply run the script by running this in a terminal```
./update_mac4lin.sh
```The script is still pretty quick and dirty, but it automates getting the update and makes sure you don't have any old files hanging around. The last step of the script opens the Appearances dialog because you will need to use the Customize button to manually select the Controls, Window Border, Icons and Pointer for the theme to work. I'm not sure why that's even needed but I hope someone will know how to fix the script.

This is actually the second script I've written so I know I'm probably missing something fairly easy. My first script was to update Sonata from svn and the process is a lot easier than it is for this script.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-03-17
Thats a great addition, Peng :) If sufficient testing is done then I can put this script up at SVN so that its available to every person who pulls down files from SVN :)

---

### Post by Plan9 on 2009-03-26
> **DJ_Peng said:**
> The last step of the script opens the Appearances dialog because you will need to use the Customize button to manually select the Controls, Window Border, Icons and Pointer for the theme to work. I'm not sure why that's even needed but I hope someone will know how to fix the script.


It's because of [FONT="Courier New"]index.theme[/FONT] in Mac4Lin_Aqua [or Graphite]. It uses names like [FONT="Courier New"]Mac4Lin_GTK_v1.0_RC[/FONT] instead of correct ones, like [FONT="Courier New"]Mac4Lin_GTK[/FONT].
Removing all [FONT="Courier New"]_v1.0_RC[/FONT] from that file (or renaming the rest of dependencies) helps.
The correct [FONT="Courier New"]index.theme[/FONT] (Aqua) should be like:
```
[Desktop Entry]
Name=Mac4Lin_Aqua
Type=X-GNOME-Metatheme
Comment=

[X-GNOME-Metatheme]
GtkTheme=Mac4Lin_GTK
MetacityTheme=Mac4Lin_GTK
IconTheme=Mac4Lin_Icons
CursorTheme=Mac4Lin_Cursors
CursorSize=32
NotificationTheme=ubuntu
```

---

### Post by phonicboom on 2009-03-29
The theme uses images to make it look the way it does. 

transparency only works for themes using solid colours and gradients set in code. 

Images are not made transparent unless you use compiz or something to make the transparency.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-03-29
> **phonicboom said:**

transparency only works for themes using solid colours and gradients set in code. 

Images are not made transparent unless you use compiz or something to make the transparency.
Yep, thats correct.

### Post by phonicboom on 2009-03-31
I don't know with the replies he's giving what he is doing, 

Does "I'm using compiz..?" mean he's using compiz? :) 

IF you are using compiz then...

CCSM -> General Options -> Opacity Settings

New -> Opacity Windows: class=Gnome-panel
-> Opacity Window Values: 25% 

but it makes everything including the text transparrent. 

OR 

you can use the panels transparrency option but it is not suitable for this theme. 

OR

this theme really does not require a transparrent panel, it is emulating something very well, very cleanly and if you want a transparnet panel then use a different more suitable theme or mix and match an alternative panel into the Mac4Lin theme so you get all the nice windows and buttons but the panel you desire ...

### Post by spandanj on 2009-03-31
hey,

I have two requests:

1) can we have 1px window border for metacity
2) can we have a proper panel theme that blends well.


thank you.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-03-31
> **spandanj said:**
> hey,

I have two requests:

1) can we have 1px window border for metacity
2) can we have a proper panel theme that blends well.


thank you.
1) Making 1px window border would require me to completely rewrite the metacity theme. I cannot assure you of when it would be done, but its definitely on my list :)
2) I don't think there is any problem with the Panel. I've coded the theme taking into consideration all the panel widgets that you may ever add. If you want transparency, I'd suggest CCSM (compiz config) as well.

The basic problem is that the pixmap engine somehow screws up images with alpha channel (transparency). Even if you manage to set a translucent Panel background (included with the theme in Panel folder), the background for the tray icons and menu bar (Apps, Sys, Places) will never be applied. It will be an ugly grey. Hence to avoid this by default I make sure the panel background is solid and integrates with the theme well.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-03-31
> **spandanj said:**
> Hey Anirudh,

Yea, if you can just make the solid panel Integrated. Right now this [screenshot] is what it looks like with the SVN version. [http://img257.imageshack.us/img257/5033/panelo.png]("http://img257.imageshack.us/img257/5033/panelo.png")

Also, can you make the shortcuts panel in nautilus wider so I can read all names completely. Please see screenshots. [http://img257.imageshack.us/img257/557/nautilusshortcutsbar.png](http://img257.imageshack.us/img257/557/nautilusshortcutsbar.png)

1) Right click on the panel > Set panel background to point at the image ~/.themes/<Mac4Lin GTK theme>/gtk-2.0/Panel/panel-bg.png

This should mitigate the problem as of now.

2) The width of the shortcut panel is not set by the gtk theme. In the screenshot you can see the 'dimple' (the circle in the center). Just drag that to the right and resize the panel :)

### Post by GeekGirl1 on 2009-05-21
I installed your .jar files by dragging them into the Tool --> Add-Ons --> Themes window. FF 3.0.10. My comments...

I'm using a widescreen monitor at 1900x1200. The Mac4Lin image in Tools -> Add-Ons --> Themes is stretched vertically. That's one funny looking penguin. The image should probably be fixed (don't scale?). My thinking is that this logo (image) is the first thing a user sees, so it's important to make a good first impression.

If you don't have a widescreen monitor, I'd suggest changing your screen resolution to match the 16:9  aspect ratio (or 16:10 for some monitors).

- The FF window frame uses the OS borders and buttons.

- Aqua and Graphite appear to be the same thing except Aqua has color. They both look very nice.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-05-22
> **spandanj said:**
> hey,

just a suggestion. two actually. Please take a look at the attached picture.

thanks.

I'm trying to get Aqua style for the drop down menu. But the problem is that the arrows on the menu are all messed up (you can see this thing in all the themes which implement aqua drop down menus). I'm yet to find a fix for it.

Secondly, the black line on the top and bottom part of the window cannot be selectively applied to certain windows. They will then stay across all the UI elements and mess things up (an e.g is if I enable the black line, then there will be a black line between the top title bar and the menu bar (File, Edit etc.). You can again take a look at this issue in some themes which implement this.

Mozilla theming is very different from GTK theming; hence many a times it very very difficult or almost impossible to port certain things from Mozilla themes to GTK. One example is the distance between buttons.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-05-27
> **noiz354 said:**
> hei

when i run 

i got this tiny message
i had created folder /.emerald/themes before

Do you use the Emerald window manager? If so, then you can manually create ~/.emerald/themes and ~/.emerald/theme folders and run the script. If you don't use Emerald then there is nothing to worry about :)

---

### Post by GeekGirl1 on 2009-05-27
Another possibility: Wrong directory, /.emerald/themes should be _~_/.emerald/themes. The '~' means your home directory.

One mistake I did was to use sudo to run the install script. This results in root owning the newly created directories which means it will fail on the next install.

I would run the installer as "normal" user and let the script invoke sudo when it needs.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-05-28
> **GeekGirl1 said:**
> One mistake I did was to use sudo to run the install script. This results in root owning the newly created directories which means it will fail on the next install.

I would run the installer as "normal" user and let the script invoke sudo when it needs.

Oh yes.. thats a good point which I don't mention in the docs/script. I will ask Peng to add this in the docs...

### Post by petit_prince on 2009-06-11
> **Plan9 said:**
> It's because of [FONT="Courier New"]index.theme[/FONT] in Mac4Lin_Aqua [or Graphite]. It uses names like [FONT="Courier New"]Mac4Lin_GTK_v1.0_RC[/FONT] instead of correct ones, like [FONT="Courier New"]Mac4Lin_GTK[/FONT].
Removing all [FONT="Courier New"]_v1.0_RC[/FONT] from that file (or renaming the rest of dependencies) helps.
The correct [FONT="Courier New"]index.theme[/FONT] (Aqua) should be like:
```
[Desktop Entry]
Name=Mac4Lin_Aqua
Type=X-GNOME-Metatheme
Comment=

[X-GNOME-Metatheme]
GtkTheme=Mac4Lin_GTK
MetacityTheme=Mac4Lin_GTK
IconTheme=Mac4Lin_Icons
CursorTheme=Mac4Lin_Cursors
CursorSize=32
NotificationTheme=ubuntu
```


DJ_Peng or infra, any chances this will get fixed anytime soon?


Cheers

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-06-13
I am happy to release Mac4Lin ver.1.0. I know it was long due. Was held up with my graduate school and work. Version 1.0 finally sees light! :) 

Changes:

* Fully supports GNOME 2.26 and backwards compatible 
* Improved support for GlobalMenu, support integrated in the default GTK theme
* Better native Xfce support
* Icon additions
* Statusbar is now fixed
* New progress bars
* New tabs
* Improved installation and uninstallation scripts
* Integrates well with Globus
* Finer UI refinements
* Metacity theme now supports different button sizes
* Firefox 3 themes are now updated
* Songbird plugins included
* Pidgin AWN 64bit plugin now included
* Fonts are now consolidated
* Transparent top panel
* GDM theme is now in-line with Mac OS X login window
* Cairo dock is the default recommended dock

Issues:

* Usplash is still buggy
* Thunderbird theme is still buggy
* GDM theme is not automatically set by the script

Screenshots:

1) Mac4Lin Desktop, NOTE:Apple logo is NOT bundled with Mac4Lin
[[IMG]http://img194.imageshack.us/img194/4125/desktop1z.th.png[/IMG]](http://img194.imageshack.us/i/desktop1z.png/)

2) Mac4Lin Desktop with Firefox
[[IMG]http://img194.imageshack.us/img194/9576/firefox1.th.png[/IMG]](http://img194.imageshack.us/i/firefox1.png/)

3) Mac4Lin Login Window
[[IMG]http://img208.imageshack.us/img208/5122/loginwindow1.th.png[/IMG]](http://img208.imageshack.us/i/loginwindow1.png/)

4) Mac4Lin with Nautilus File Manager
[[IMG]http://img208.imageshack.us/img208/7973/nautilus1.th.png[/IMG]](http://img208.imageshack.us/i/nautilus1.png/)

5) Mac4Lin with Rhythmbox
[[IMG]http://img208.imageshack.us/img208/2024/rhythmbox1.th.png[/IMG]](http://img208.imageshack.us/i/rhythmbox1.png/)

6) Mac4Lin with Terminal
[[IMG]http://img196.imageshack.us/img196/3985/terminal1.th.png[/IMG]](http://img196.imageshack.us/i/terminal1.png/)

7) Mac4Lin on Xfce!
[[IMG]http://img208.imageshack.us/img208/9921/xfce1.th.png[/IMG]](http://img208.imageshack.us/i/xfce1.png/)

It is available for download at Mac4Lin Sourceforge.net [Download page]("https://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=204373") with immediate effect. Grab your copy now!

I am eagerly waiting for the Sourceforge.net Community Awards 2009.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-06-16
> **teolemon said:**
> No trouble, just that the ressemblance is near perfect with Coverflow :-)
Cool :)

> **prvul said:**
> Great theme! Although i am not a mac fan, i must say: "THIS LOOKS AWSOME!"
Thank you :)

> **abhilashm86 said:**
> these were those errors, should i enable metacity compulsory or what??
also i dragged firefox jar to addons and did it.............
The only error I see is that you don't use Emerald yet you selected 'Yes' during the install script. No wonder it threw up an error. Secondly, do you use Compiz or xcompmgr? If so, then you don't need metacity compositor. One of these 3 compositors is required for AWN or Cairo Dock. Without these you will not haf any kind of dock. If you are unsure, just say no to this question and let the installation continue. If you are unable to use the dock, then run the install script again and say 'yes' to this question.

> **neal.m.master said:**
> This looks pretty cool.  A couple of questions:  

Does this slow anything down?  It seems like the graphics would be far more intense than the default GNOME.  

Also, when will a stable version be out?  I appreciate that people are using it and letting others know about their problems, but I'd rather wait until it works (nearly) perfectly.  

Lastly, is there an uninstall script?  If you change your mind is it just as simple to go back?
1) I haf never seen Mac4Lin slow down the system. Yes, if you benchmark it, it may slow down by few 'microseconds'! :P Rest assured and go use it!

2) The stable version is out! 1.0 is the stable version. What made you believe otherwise? :D

3) Yes, there is an uninstall script which will roll back the UI to the default Ubuntu one.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-06-24
I'm very happy to announce that Mac4Lin has been declared as one of the finalists at Sourceforge.net Community Awards 2009 in the Best Visual Design category. The final phase of voting began today and will run till July 20th 2009. Please vote for Mac4Lin, if you feel it deserves to be voted. To vote click on this image: 

[[IMG]http://sf.net/awards/cca/badge_img.php?f=414[/IMG]]("http://sf.net/community/cca09/vote/?f=414")

Optionally, you can also click on the first box in the right frame on my [blog]("http://phoenix-ani.blogspot.com"). You do not need to Sourceforge.net login id. All you need is a valid email id. Each vote is associated with an email id, which needs confirmation that you actually voted (you will get an email giving a confirmation link, so all you need to do is click it). The whole voting process takes just 3 clicks.

I urge patrons to vote for Mac4Lin if they feel it should win. Mac4Lin is completing with projects like Xbox Media Center (XBMC) etc. I once again thank everyone for their continued support, feedback and appreciation. Mac4Lin exists today because of you all :) Do spread the word around about this.

### Post by Plan9 on 2009-06-28
If I could suggest something.
After installing 1.0 the top menu-bar has lost its singularity, same as you can see on screen-shot [here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7472069&postcount=691").

Setting the background of gnome-panel to Menu-Menubar/menubar.png fixed it.

### Post by GeekGirl1 on 2009-07-05
OK, thanks. In the mean time, I managed to install GlobalMenu.  Note that all references from the 1.0_RC2 doc are now deprecated and should point to here: [http://code.google.com/p/gnome2-globalmenu/](http://code.google.com/p/gnome2-globalmenu/) I was confused because it says "Mac4Lin now officially supports Globalmenu and Gloobus", so I was looking for some sort of installation in the download package. None found.

The install went OK and it looks good. Be sure to do a step-by-step description of how you position it on the taskbar panel and what to expect after the install. What I didn't expect:

-That you can click on the title to show the active windows. Show desktop, open apps, etc. It's not obvious.
-All menus now appear on the taskbar panel. That means that they will disappear from your active windows. Gone. I don't have a Mac and it took me a while to figure this out. I hope they reappear if I uninstall it...

I also got Cairo-Dock running with the Mac OSX Leopard theme from gnome-look.org: [http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/MacOSX+Leopard+Cairo-Dock+Theme?content=89410](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/MacOSX+Leopard+Cairo-Dock+Theme?content=89410) No Cairo-dock install software found in the download package.

Minor note: Be sure to update the SourceForge website listed in your upcoming PDF docs. The 1.0_RC2 version shows [http://sourceforge.net/project/mac4lin/](http://sourceforge.net/project/mac4lin/), should be [http://sourceforge.net/project](http://sourceforge.net/project)_s_/mac4lin/ (/project should be /projects)

You might also be interested to know that the FF (3.0.11) and Thunderbird themes work just fine in Win XP. I'm sharing profiles, so the Mac4Lin themes are used there as well.

I know I'm adding to your workload, but the fact that you did a really good explanation for 1.0_RC2 in the PDF was enough incentive for me to continue to use Mac4Lin vs. "something else".

I'll be looking for your updates. I really like this interface.
