### Post by GeekGirl1 on 2009-07-07
I have recovered my NVidia drivers. A screenshot is attached. This is a wide-screen display @ 1920 x 1200 resolution. I optimized the font rendering (you can't do that in Win XP!).

Description of my Desktop:
- The Gnome footprint icon is at the very left. I am indecisive about letting this icon remain or to replace with the apple icon. I want to make the "transformation" complete, but I like the footprint.
- GlobalMenu is positioned on the top left.
- On the top right is my "problem". The wired icon is "paired" with the Keyboard Accessibility Status icon. Perhaps I don't understand how to update the system panel. I can't remove it.
- Just below the taskbar (right side) is the Add to Panel dialog box which shows all the icons. I don't see any matching Network applets, but I think it's part of the Notification Area applet. Clicking on Notification Area has no effect when I try to add it to another panel.
- One comment on these panel icons - I prefer to use the "logout" icon for Shutdown. As you can see, the knob is much too shiny for the taskbar. Since this is a single-user PC, I use Shutdown most of the time. Can you update the Shutdown icon to change the background closer to Logout? Or, perhaps to allow me to swap the icons (how?). I will defer my preferences to the Mac OS implementation.

On the bottom is Cairo-Dock. I installed a theme marked "(user) Mac OSX". I have no idea where or when I installed this, as I was experimenting with several themes at gnome-look.org (?). If it was included with Cairo-Dock, this is good.

You can see the cursor is focused on my NVidia GPU temperature monitor. Very nice.

I did not like the Accessories -> Terminal applet for these reasons (Cairo-Dock screen shot attached):
- The transparency was very distracting
- When I wanted to exit the shell, it automatically restarted a new one. That is not the correct behavior. It forces the user to terminate the window instead of "exit". My thinking is that anyone who is using bash (or csh, etc.) is expecting the shell to operate as expected. It is very inconvenient and encourages bad behavior of the user. In the case of the last shell "exit", the window should close.
- The Terminal icon is low resolution and appears to be poor quality in comparison to the other icons.
- The Terminal is attached to the dock and is very limited in it's display properties. Perhaps this default behavior can be modified.

I am using the gnome-terminal (2nd icon from the left) in place of Terminal. Very nice icon, but I think it should look closer to a "terminal" with high resolution quality. Perhaps an LCD panel would be more appropriate? :)

Firefox is the compass icon (4th icon from the left). How can I replace it with the correct icon?

fabounet - For your information, I do not own a Mac. I think the Mac OS has the best GUI design. I am not the Mac4Lin developer, but I would like to have a perfect theme available. (Merci de l'offre...)

---

I did not like the Accessories -> Terminal applet for these reasons (Cairo-Dock screen shot attached):
- The transparency was very distracting
- When I wanted to exit the shell, it automatically restarted a new one. That is not the correct behavior. It forces the user to terminate the window instead of "exit". My thinking is that anyone who is using bash (or csh, etc.) is expecting the shell to operate as expected. It is very inconvenient and encourages bad behavior of the user. In the case of the last shell "exit", the window should close.
- The Terminal icon is low resolution and appears to be poor quality in comparison to the other icons.

Thanks for the screenshots. I will go thru the points one by one.

1) If you feel like changing the gnome foot to something else, you can get the step by step procedure to do that on Mac4Lin sourceforge.net forums.

2) The wired icon is paired with the accessibility icon coz both are present in the system tray (or the notification area) and are not individual applets. You cannot separate them. You can probably hide the keyboard accessibility icon from showing up there.

3) You can prolly install Network Monitor applet. The problem with Network manager is that with every release they make about 100 changes and it breaks the whole thing. I'm really tired of updating tens of icons every time, hence I've decided to boycott NM!!!

4) You can replace the shutdown icon to whatever icon you want. Just head to ~/.icons/<Mac4Lin Icon folder>/scalable/apps and look for the shiny shutdown icon. I'm myself considering replacing the current shutdown icon with something else.

5) Thats the default theme which comes with Cairo Dock

6) The terminal applet doesn't play nice with Mac4Lin. I need to look into this. I can only make changes to the appearance and not the behavior. Maybe you can file a bug at Cairo dock forums.

7) Looks like the terminal applet doesn't grab icons from the active icon theme instead uses the default gnome terminal icon. You can try right clicking it and pointing to a custom icon. Mac4Lin Icon theme has a nice black LCD terminal icon. You can do that for the other icons on the dock too. Almost every icon is present in the Mac4Lin pack.

I'm striving to take Mac4Lin as close to perfection as possible. But there are many limitations in GTK which don't allow me to port the exact Mac OS X UI to the same.

---

### Post by fabounet on 2009-07-08
about the terminal applet :
you can of course set up the background color (including transparency)
the default size if also configurable

But you can also choose to detach it from the dock, and for instance put it on the Widget Layer and call it back with a shortcut (by default, I think it's ctrl+F4 or something like that)
That makes something like Tilda but with tabs (you can also rename tabs and assigne theme a color)

you can also change the applet's icon you don't like the default one. Be sure to have the last version of the dock since a little bug was preventing to do it a few weeks ago.

About the McOSX theme that I see on your screenshot, it's probably the one present in the list of the dock's Theme-Manager.
It's definitely not a perfect theme, and I'd love to see someone who knows MacOSX making it look closer to the original Dock. ;-)

### Post by GeekGirl1 on 2009-07-29
Hint: If you run the entire script as superuser (sudo), it will install the configuration files in your home directory as root. You'll need to go to those directories as superuser and chown them back to your normal username.

I found that the right way to install everything is to run as yourself, the script will invoke sudo where needed. At that point, the script will stop and ask for the root password.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-07-31
Looks like the 3 basic directories are missing! Try doing this:

1) mkdir ~/.themes
2) mkdir ~/.icons
3) mkdir ~/.emerald

And then try to run the script again.

### Post by Firestrider on 2009-08-01
Fresh install again... 

First I installed avant window navigator and emerald.
Second I opened a terminal and put in those three lines:
mkdir ~/.themes
mkdir ~/.icons
mkdir ~/.emerald
Then I got the package and extracted it on desktop and ran in terminal:
sean@sean-laptop ~ $ cd ~/Desktop/Mac4Lin_Install_v1.0
sean@sean-laptop ~/Desktop/Mac4Lin_Install_v1.0 $ ./Mac4Lin_Install_v1.0.sh

The script finished without any errors. I then restarted the computer and got back to desktop. The only thing that seemed enabled was the icons, windows border theme, and login screen. 

Desktop background wasn't there, sounds aren't there, panel is not laid out correctly or transparent, AWN theme wasn't applied, etc.

What is done by the script and what has to be done manually?

It's part of why I went with the combination of GlobalMenu/AWN/Google Gadgets Sidebar/Screenlets for my desktop. It may suck up more resources but I love how it makes my desktop look.

### Post by fabounet on 2009-09-11
Here is my little contribution to the documentation of Mac4Lin (this is the reviewed part about Cairo-Dock).
Thanks in advance to integration this in your document.
You can of course re-arrange it the way you want. :-)

[HTML]chapter 13
Cairo-Dock is the most MacOSX-like dock you can find on Linux : it features the original zoom effect, and run with OpenGL, making it very smooth and saving your CPU, just as the original OSX Dock. It also has a dedicated theme that mimics the original one, and the common applets found in the Mac dock like Stack.
It also proposes a fake transparency mode, which allows it to run on old computers.

Installing Cairo-Dock
It probably exists in your distribution, but it is always better to have the latest version, since it offers new features and improvements. Anyway, be sure to have Cairo-Dock2, which is the only maintained version, and the plug-ins.
To get the latest stable version, we recommend you to use the project's repository : http://www.cairo-dock.org/ww_page.php?p=By%20distributions&lang=en. You will then automatically be up-to-date each time a new version is released.
If you want the cutting edge of Cairo-Dock, the project is located on LaunchPad and has its own PPA; there you can grab the current BZR sources, and the weekly build. See http://www.cairo-dock.org/ww_page.php?p=Accueil&lang=en#0-Installation for more information.

Running Cairo-Dock
In your Application Menu, go to System, and choose either GLX-Dock or Cairo-Dock.
GLX-Dock runs the OpenGL backend, that is to say it is hardware accelerated, making it extremely smooth and providing cool animations and special effects.
To run GLX-Dock, you need to have either an nVidia card (preferably with the latest nVidia drivers), or an Intel/ATI card (with the latest X server that you can find in Ubuntu Karmic for instance).
See the wiki if you experience some troubles.
If your graphic card does not support the OpenGL backend, you can run the cairo backend by choosing the other entry in the menu.

Adding Cairo-Dock on auto-start.
Simply right-click on the dock -> cairo-dock -> launch on startup.
If it doesn't work with your distribution, use the appropriate tool to add a program on startup, and fill the command option with "cairo-dock -o" to run GLX-Dock or "cairo-dock -c" to run without OpenGL.

Getting themes and the OSX look'n'feel
There is nothing to install, Cairo-Dock comes with a Theme-Manager that can download themes on the Net : right-click on the dock -> cairo-dock -> Manage themes.
For a Mac style desktop, choose the theme named "MacOSX", check the 2 little boxes, and apply; you're done !

Customizing your dock
Cairo-Dock is highly customizable. The Configuration panel will let you transform it as you wish : right-click on the dock -> cairo-dock -> Configure.
You might want to read this tutorial to get start with customization : http://www.cairo-dock.org/ww_page.php?p=Tutorial-Customisation&lang=en
Also, there is an useful help available directly in the dock : right-click on the dock -> cairo-dock -> Help.

Adding Widgets on your desktop (Desklets) and using the Widget Layer
All the applets of Cairo-Dock are detachable and can live on your desktop; simply drag an appet out of the dock.
If you're running Compiz, you can set them on the Widget Layer : right-click on the desklet -> Accessibility -> On widget layer.
The dock will automatically add the rule "class=Cairo-dock & type=utility" to your Compiz settings.
You can also make a desklet be on top or below other windows.
You eigher can make a widget bar : detach some applets, set their accessibility to "reserve space", and place them on a side of your screen.
This is very useful to have a clean dock and a nice desktop.

While we support both Cairo-Dock and AWN, we recommend the use of Cairo-Dock.

chapter 14
Alternative widget layers
Cairo-Dock : the applets of this dock can also live on your desktop ! Simply drag and drop an appet out of the dock.
See paragraph 13.1 for more details.

chapter 16
Exaile plug-in - Cairo-dock
Cairo-dock comes with a MusicPlayer applet since the version 2.1, that lets you control almost any music player, including Exaile; it handles controls, cover display and notifications.
Open the config panel of the dock, and check the box of the applet to activate it.
Then click on its buton to to edit the options of the applet, go to the Configuration tab, select the player of your choice, and apply.
If your player is already launched, you can also right-click on the applet and choose "detect the player".
You can detach the applet and place it on your desktop if you prefer.[/HTML]

Edit : the html wrappers dont do line wrapping, it's quite awful to scroll horizontally, sorry for that ^_^

---

### Post by jeannacav on 2009-09-11
> **DJ_Peng said:**
> I don't recall how Finder works from a UI perspective, but how does [Tux Commander]("http://tuxcmd.sourceforge.net/") compare? Someone mentioned it in the [Cool Apps thread]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7924892&postcount=1724") yesterday. I think I had it on my comp in the past but I don't have it installed now. I'd be willing to install it and see how it plays with M4L 1.0 if it's a better option for M4L users  than Nautilus.

Thanks dj peng (also infrared),
tuxcommand won't do it as it is.

This column thing is just a hybrid of the list view and the icon view.

It works just like  icons except that the display is in alphabetical list form. (and you only need to singleclick it)

The way this works should be no more difficult to program than (conceptually) changing the next nested folder into a list and that list is then displayed in a vertical window/panel/column to the right with scroll bars that show up if necessary like any other window. The width is default narrower than a normal window, and there can be more window/panels created as needed.

This way, you can drill very deep into your files and yet still see exactly where they came from... at a glance.

I have been doing a lot of research in the past few years and I have generated an immense number of folders and files. In doing research, one doesn't know ahead of time where anything will go.

This year a new person joined our group. She read all the relevant threads 2 times before even announcing her presence, but had some questions. I knew the answers in my head, but to save thousands of words etc, I needed pix and other references.

I spent no more than 20 minutes scanning literally thousands of files and folders in a big range of areas on my mac. I was able to provide the answers needed and then continued with my work.

In no way would I have been able to do this on either list or icon form.

I believe most people have not tried it. I only tried it out of curiosity because apple had praised it and asked people to give it a week. It took less than a week to realize the benefit. It is very intuitive and ... I need it.

I hope someone who has the programming skills can help with this!!

thank you,

jeanna

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-09-12
Thanks, jeannacav. Now I understand the appeal of Finder a bit better.
> **jeannacav said:**
> I spent no more than 20 minutes scanning literally thousands of files and folders in a big range of areas on my mac. I was able to provide the answers needed and then continued with my work.

In no way would I have been able to do this on either list or icon form.
Damn, that sounds nice. No wonder I've seen so many people asking for it.

I did some searching, on both with [Uboontu]("http://uboontu.com/") and with Crunchbang's [Ubuntu Search Engine]("http://crunchbang.org/ubuntu-search-engine/"), and was able to find something that may help. A comment on the thread [Is there anyway to get a column view (like Finder) in Nautilus?]("http://ubuntu-virginia.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1247839") has a mention of [Pygoscelis]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=415461"). Unfortunately, as some readers of the thread in the previous link, there's no way to download Pygoscelis from it's [SourceForge site]("http://pygoscelis.sourceforge.net/"), but I was able to find a link to download the alpha realease source code on [GnomeFiles]("http://gnomefiles.org/app.php/Pygoscelis"). As I perused the info on Pygoscelis via the SF main page (starting [here]("https://sourceforge.net/projects/pygoscelis/")) I saw comparisons to the [GNOME Commander]("http://www.nongnu.org/gcmd/"), which may be another option and is available in the [Ubuntu universe repo]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/en/jaunty/gnome-commander").

You may want to file a feature request either on Launchpad or on [GNOME's Bugzilla]("https://bugzilla.gnome.org/") to request that this feature be brought to Nautilus. If you do please let us know so we can subscribe to the bug and vote for it to help the devs know how many people would like to see this kind of file management in Nautilus.

### Post by jeannacav on 2009-09-15
Hi everybody,

I just discovered something that might work in place of the full columns...

Then it could be made better by infrareddude or someone else.

The file where I stored that avatar gif last night was somehow stored under the rest of a list of still empty files of the 'file browser'.

When I doubleclicked it the file opened and the listed buttons were showing the parentage of this file.
Now, maybe this was an update I missed but this behavior only happened on the icon view when the file was opened and NOT the list view when I was just looking.

So, I changed the behavior of the list-icon to open on a single click.
Now, a singleclick takes me down the child levels and because the files/folders are opening, there is a button showing the parentage. This is still not as great as having the whole list of parents stay visible in one column each, but with the parent name showing on the browser, I think I can manage.

So, this is in the regular nautilus file manager, and that means mac4lin, will work as it is supposed to.

I will try it out.

jeanna

### Post by jeannacav on 2009-09-16
> **infra_red_dude said:**
> The screenshots helped. But this is not actually what you want, right? That will only expand the tree and give you a second column, thats it. Not like Finder, where you can virtually dig unlimited levels deep.

MMM hard to describe.
open up the second one because it shows both.
They are both list view.
The way I opened the file path on the left is the conventional way... to click on the arrow. This quickly gets hard to navigate because I have so many items in a folder.
Note in the buttons bar there is only one button identifying where I am - the 'Ginala' home button even though I dug down 3 more levels.


The one on the right is ALSO list view.
Note that the button bar contains a button for each folder I opened to get there.
You can see my cursor pointing to the second of 4 folders listed.

Now,
The difference is that in the 'column view' of the finder, there is a whole list instead of just the button.

The way it seems to happen to the user, is as a folder is opened, the list remains where it is and a new window forms -not on top, but - to the right of the chosen folder. This is the column and it is just a narrow window and it continues to be in list view. If necessary, there is a scroll bar that appears with it. - It really behaves like a regular window in all ways. But it is narrow by default and appears immediately next to the previous one.
A scroll bar appears at the bottom when the columns exceed the normal width of the original window.
There can be infinite columns that form because they are made when needed by the fact that a folder contains items in it.

As I said, even though it isn't all of what I want, this will do better than GWorkspace, because this works in nautilus.

I said a lot in the hope that I answered your question, because, I wasn't exactly sure what your question was.

Oh the other thing I can do on my mac is I can add a color to the name of the folder so I can see it easier.
On my mac
Sciencemisc is 1 click on the scrollbar to get me to where it is and Joulethief is 3 clicks on the scrollbar.
This is less important, but a great feature in a list 156 items long.

thank you,

jeanna

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2009-10-09
> **pickarooney said:**
> I'm using Xubuntu 9.04
Hmm.. till the previous version of GNOME, the "don't display icons" setting could be set in the gtkrc file which means that GNOME/Xfce and other GTK based DE don't display icons. However, from the recent version, this setting was shifted to the gconf editor. Since it applies to GNOME, I believe, no wonder you are seeing the icons on buttons.

Do you know if Xfce has a central register like gconf for storing settings?

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-12-21
My bad. We discovered that we no longer need separate themes for the GlobalMenu. You can use the regular themes (Mac4Lin_GTK_Graphite_v1.0 or Mac4Lin_Meta_v1.0) whether you use the GlobalMenu or not. I should have updated that part of the docs before they went live.

*Edit 8:08 am EST:* The GlobalMenu change was already made in the docs. From page 8:
> Past versions included themes labeled MacMenu, but the current themes work both with and without the GlobalMenu (formerly known as the MacMenu hack) so you no longer need to worry about which theme you activate beyond your choice of aqua and graphite color schemes. 

I also have another edit to make to the docs that has been on my todo list. I've got the .odt file open now so I can try to find all the edits I still need to make. If I'm lucky infra will have the update for publication later today.

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-12-26
While getting caught up with the monthly screenshot thread I came across a post by yahrialb with a very nice look. It turns out he uses [GnoMenu]("https://launchpad.net/gnomenu"), a great consolidated menu app that has some pretty nice [themeing]("http://gnome-look.org/index.php?xcontentmode=189") capabilities and also works pretty nicely with AWN and Cairo Dock, although I need to check on how to change the AWN applet icon. I decided that while I found a nice [Apple Start Button]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Apple+Start+Button?content=116747") available it just doesn't work as well with the Mac4Lin GTK themes. Making a new GnoMenu button is so easy I quickly ginned up a Mac4Lin button for GnoMenu but before I posted it to Gnome-Look I wanted to post it here and ask anyone who uses GnoMenu to please try my button and see how it works for you.

I'll see about making a Mac4Lin GnoMenu theme as well, or at least an icon theme for it. I'll also see if there's a way to change the AWN applet icon as well.

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2010-01-14
Actually you can grab a screenshot even with the menu closing when it loses focus. Go into the Take Screenshot panel and set a delay (Grab after a delay of ## seconds). Then click the Take Screenshot button and while the delay is counting down bring up the GnoMenu. That should get a screenshot with the menu itself, as shown in my attachment (taken for my posting in the monthly screenshot thread if I can ever customize an icon theme to use a combination of icons from a couple of themes.

I usually go for a 5-10 second delay when I'm getting a screenshot of something I have to bring up.

As far as using the active system icon theme goes, right click on the GnoMenu icon and select Preferences, then go to the Preferences tab and check the 4th box, Use system icons instead of theme icons. No, that's not the Mac4Lin icons showing in my screenshot, which is why I need to gin up a new theme that uses a combination of Mac4Lin icons and other icons.

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2010-01-15
> **ThePantryMaster said:**
> The screenshot info was top notch, cheers dude.

[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Baghira-leopard%28menu+and+button%29?content=105505]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Baghira-leopard%28menu+and+button%29?content=105505")

Found that, it doesn't install the way it should, although I'm sure it can be done manually.  I can't be bothered though as it doesn't look as functional.

Is there a mac bluetooth icon for the top bar?  and one for the compiz fusion icon.  Oh and battery too?

Edit: that leopard menu, the menu and the button are in the same compressed file, extract them and install the menu individually.  (it's not great though)  And how do I get the quit button looking like OS-X, without the username etc?

I managed to get the Baghira theme installed without much trouble. Did you extract the files from the downloaded .tar.gz? There's the theme and the button in the downloaded tar.gz, and from there you should be able to install Baghira.tar.gz without a hitch. If not let me know and I can see about attaching the theme file on my system.

I'm not totally thrilled with the Baghira theme myself. Usually I use the Kore theme myself, mainly because I don't like the layout of the Blue or Glass theme. I did make a Mac4Lin GnoMenu button that I may have posted here before (I can't recall). I'll attach it here, and once I can get confirmation that it works for someone else I'll post it on GNOME-Look. To install it simply get into the GnoMenu prefs, then click the Install button in the Button Selection area. Navigate to the Mac4Lin GnoMenu Button.tar.gz file (you may need to provide your sudo password, but I can't be 100% sure), then simply click Open. Once you see the dialog saying that it was installed select it from the Button Selection dropdown menu and click Ok. Let GnoMenu restart and you'll have the Mac4Lin distro icon as your GnoMenu icon.

I think we added a fusion icon in the 1.0 icon theme, but if not you should be able to use the icon that comes with the package. I can't say about the Bluetooth icon (I don't use it on my system) but I believe there is a battery icon.

For the Quit button to lose the user name you need to remove the User Switcher applet and use the Shut Down... applet. It doesn't provide a way to log off a user but it will give you a button to shut down, restart or hibernate your system.

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2010-01-20
For anyone trying to figure out why the icon for network manager apps (and applets) is so bloody huge I finally tracked down a solution. The icon is located in ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0/scalable/apps/22 as connect_established.png, nm-adhoc.png, nm-device-wired.png and nm-device-wireless.png. I'm not sure which one is actually used, but all of them are system linked to ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0/scalable/apps/connect_established.png (attached below), which measures 128x128, the normal size for icons in that directory.

I was able to resize the icon to 22x22 and save it as ~/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0/scalable/apps/22/connect_established.png, and I created linked files with the other names in that directory, all linking to the 22x22 version of connect_established.png. As soon as the linked files were created I opened the AWN Settings app and saw that the icon was in fact changed to the proper 22x22 size.

I'm attaching my resized icon, as well as the XCF files (22x22 as well as the larger 128x128 sized image) I used to make the new icon. Fee free to tweak, correct, or otherwise improve the icons.

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2010-03-29
I've made a pair of Emerald themes to go with the new Radiance theme for lucid. Before I post them to Gnome-Look could someone test them to make sure they look right?

The first is the Mac4Lin Radiance Emerald Theme, with the "traffic light" buttons the way Mac4Lin users expect them to be aligned.
[IMG]http://nancib.files.wordpress.com/2010/03/mac4lin-radiance-emerald-theme-screenshot.png?w=300[/IMG]

The second, "B" version moves the buttons to the opposite side, as has been the default location for Karmic on back.
[IMG]http://nancib.files.wordpress.com/2010/03/mac4lin-radiance-emerald-b-theme-screenshot.png?w=300[/IMG]

**Credit where credit's due**
This theme was made after trying out the [Elementary elegante (lucid version)]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Elementary+elegante+(lucid+version)?content=121717") Emerald theme and finding the buttons flat didn't work on my system. The theme was made using the colors of the [Pint - Radiance theme]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Pint+-+Ambiance+%26+Radiance?content=121143"), combined with buttons from the Mac4Lin theme as well as from Merman's great [Elementary Modified]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Elementary+Modified?content=106491") theme.

Once I can confirm that there are no major edits needed to these themes I'll post them to Gnome-Look.org so others can enjoy them. I also have a blog post about the themes all written and just waiting for them to go onto Gnome-Look before my post is published. Thanks for all your help.

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2010-09-12
Just an update, Mac4Lin SVN has been updated with a new version of GTK Themes' and GTK Icons' directories. They are compatible with the latest version of GNOME and distributions like Ubuntu, Fedora etc.

To download everything goto this page: [http://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net/viewvc/mac4lin/](http://mac4lin.svn.sourceforge.net/viewvc/mac4lin/) and on the botton click on "Download Tarball". If you however want to download specific components (like GTK_Theme etc.) then goto that directory and download the specific tarball. To install, you can follow any guide available online to install either the GTK theme or the GTK Icon theme.

I am yet to make a formal release, but those who want to experiment with the latest version and file bugs are welcome to do so :)

---

### Post by Tsui Pen on 2010-12-13
I couldn't find a solution to my huge wi-fi icon anywhere so I decided to give it a go myself.

This is how I fixed it:

1. nano index.theme (located in /home/user/.icons/Mac4Lin_Icons_v1.0/)
2. added:

[scalable/status]
Size=22
Context=Status
Type=Scalable

3. ctrl + x and save.
4. Log out and back in.

I should note that I'm using Debian Lenny, but I came here because there is little to no support for Mac4Lin on this distro. However, I'm not sure it makes that much of a difference.

I'm off to work on the goofy-looking taskbar.

---

### Post by infra_red_dude on 2011-01-07
